        $(window).scroll(function(){

       <div class="widget Blog" id="Blog1">
        <div class="post">
         <div class="entry-container">
          <div class="entry-content">
           <h1>
            The Discount Rate Isn't a Monetary Policy Move, Fed Swears
            <div class="meta1">
             <p>
              <small>
               <span>
                <i class="fa fa-clock-o">
                </i>
                Monday, February 22, 2010
               </span>
               <span>
                <i class="fa fa-tags">
                </i>
                <span class="label-info">
                 <a href="http://www.jrdeputyaccountant.com/search/label/discount%20rate" rel="tag">
                  discount rate
                 </a>
                 ,
                 <a href="http://www.jrdeputyaccountant.com/search/label/elizabeth%20duke" rel="tag">
                  elizabeth duke
                 </a>
                 ,
                 <a href="http://www.jrdeputyaccountant.com/search/label/fed%20exit%20strategy" rel="tag">
                  fed exit strategy
                 </a>
                 ,
                 <a href="http://www.jrdeputyaccountant.com/search/label/fed%20governors" rel="tag">
                  fed governors
                 </a>
                 ,
                 <a href="http://www.jrdeputyaccountant.com/search/label/monetary%20policy" rel="tag">
                  monetary policy
                 </a>
                 ,
                 <a href="http://www.jrdeputyaccountant.com/search/label/NY%20Fed" rel="tag">
                  NY Fed
                 </a>
                </span>
               </span>
               <i class="fa fa-comments">
               </i>
               2 Comments
              </small>
             </p>
            </div>
           </h1>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_azimCSzqNnc/S4IfuVcdsUI/AAAAAAAAEhw/wSrLVUmnJpI/s1600-h/IMG00578-20100221-1719.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5440946180707955010" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_azimCSzqNnc/S4IfuVcdsUI/AAAAAAAAEhw/wSrLVUmnJpI/s320/IMG00578-20100221-1719.jpg" style="display: block; margin: 0px auto 10px; text-align: center; cursor: pointer; width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           That's really funny because I have this comic book in front of me called "
           <span style="font-style: italic;">
            The Story of the Federal Reserve System
           </span>
           " that is jam-packed with bad art and a reference to the discount rate that says the exact opposite. "Still another tool of monetary policy involves the discount rate..."
           <span style="font-style: italic;">
            <span style="font-weight: bold;">
             They
            </span>
           </span>
           wrote it, not me. (you can
           <a href="https://www.newyorkfed.org/publications/result.cfm?comics=1">
            get your copy directly from FRBNY
           </a>
           , I've got plenty I'll be using as shredded bedding for my hamster
           <a href="http://sfappeal.com/news/2010/02/worth-the-3-todays-print-only-chronicles-good-bad-and-ugly.php">
            if the SF Chronicle shrinks any smaller
           </a>
           )
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Wait a second, Bill Dudley's own NY Fed published this crap, does he know what he's saying?
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://blogs.wsj.com/economics/2010/02/19/dudley-calls-discount-rate-change-technical/?utm_source=feedburner&amp;utm_medium=feed&amp;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+wsj%2Feconomics%2Ffeed+%28WSJ.com%3A+Real+Time+Economics+Blog%29">
            WSJ's Real Time Economics
           </a>
           :
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <blockquote>
            Federal Reserve Bank of New York President William Dudley said Friday the increase in the discount rate done by the central bank late Thursday was technical in nature.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            We made a very small technical change by raising the discount rate, Dudley said. The action yesterday was really an action about the improvement in banks, and reflected the fact these institutions no longer need this emergency source of cheap funding the way they did during the depths of the financial crisis, the official said.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            The discount rate increase is not at all a signal of any imminent tightening in monetary policy, and the Feds commitment to keep rates very low for an extended period is still very much in place, Dudley said.
           </blockquote>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           I'm sure he does. If not, his Fed colleagues are happy to chirp in and reiterate the point to calm the crackheads hooked on easy money.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Fed Governor Elizabeth Duke took a moment from
           <a href="http://www.federalreserve.gov/newsevents/speech/duke20100218a.htm">
            waxing poetic over her first year at the Fed
           </a>
           to back up her homie Dudley on the point that the discount rate move is more, well,
           <span style="font-style: italic;">
            show
           </span>
           than anything else.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           So what is it? Tightening? Faking it?
           <a href="http://blogs.wsj.com/economics/2010/02/18/feds-duke-discount-rate-hike-not-signaling-any-monetary-policy-change/?utm_source=feedburner&amp;utm_medium=feed&amp;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+wsj%2Feconomics%2Ffeed+%28WSJ.com%3A+Real+Time+Economics+Blog%29">
            To hear Duke tell it, it's just to remind everyone that the Fed is no one's bitch
           </a>
           . Ooooh, I'm shaking in my Pumas over here.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <blockquote>
            Id emphasize that the changes are simply a reversal of the spread reduction we made to combat stigma and like the closure of a number of extraordinary credit programs earlier this month, represent further normalization of the Federal Reserves lending facilities; they do not signal any change in the outlook for monetary policy and are not expected to lead to tighter financial conditions for households and businesses, Duke said in her prepared remarks.
           </blockquote>
           <br/>
           So that other tool for monetary policy that the Fed's own propaganda pushes? Forget about it.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           They attached
           <a href="http://www.federalreserve.gov/Releases/H41/Current/">
            their balance sheet
           </a>
           to the announcement just in case you didn't know they're already in a shit load of trouble with no way out. That was nice of them, eh?
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="clear">
         </div>
         <div class="entry-meta clearfix">
          <div class="up_arrow">
          </div>
          <div class="pull-right share-story-container">

            Pinky Swear
said...
           </div>
           <div class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-815844247604554887">
            <p>
             How publicly to characterize the discount rate and reserve requirements is a contentious issue within the Fed because until recently they let open-market operations do all the work and tried to cancel out the effects of anything else. Realistically, the discount rate is a monetary policy tool, but for now anyway not much of one.
            </p>

       <div class="widget BlogArchive" id="BlogArchive1">
        <h2>
         The Chatter
        </h2>
        <div class="widget-content">
         <div id="ArchiveList">
          <div id="BlogArchive1_ArchiveList">
